Comparing to **CC(C)OC(=O)C** (isopropyl acetate):
- Isopropyl acetate has only 5 carbons total and a branched structure, with a property value of -0.84030639.
- Ethyl hexanoate has more carbons (8 vs. 5) and longer chains, so it should be less polar and have a less negative (or more positive) property value than isopropyl acetate.

### Step 4: Estimate the Property Value
Based on the trends:
- The property value increases (becomes less negative or more positive) with increasing carbon chain length in esters, likely due to increasing hydrophobicity.
- Ethyl hexanoate, with 8 total carbons, falls between isopropyl acetate (5 carbons, -0.84030639) and methyl nonanoate (10 carbons, 0.05775797) in terms of molecular size and alkyl chain length.

I can estimate the property value by interpolating between these two reference points:
- Difference in carbon count between isopropyl acetate (5C) and methyl nonanoate (10C): 5 carbons.
- Difference in property value: 0.05775797 - (-0.84030639) = 0.89806436.
- Change in property value per carbon: 0.89806436 / 5 ≈ 0.1796.
- Ethyl hexanoate has 8 carbons, so from isopropyl acetate (5C), it’s an increase of 3 carbons.
- Estimated property value increase: 3 * 0.1796 ≈ 0.5388.
- Property value for ethyl hexanoate: -0.84030639 + 0.5388 ≈ -0.3015.

However, I note that the relationship may not be strictly linear, as the effect of additional carbons might diminish with longer chains. Comparing to other non-ester molecules with similar carbon counts (e.g., **CCCCCCCI**, property -0.03408113, with 7 carbons), the value is closer to zero, but the presence of the ester group in ethyl hexanoate likely makes it more polar than an alkyl halide, suggesting a slightly more negative value.
